  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5298473b-e3bf-47f5-9521-b0aa1c76b82d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<a href="/questions/1239807-can-it-be-read-enjoyed-without-reading">Can it be read &amp; enjoyed without reading any of the previous books in the saga?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>

<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1239807'><a id="like_count_community_question_1239807" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1239807?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F68483.The_Vor_Game">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/6944024-maynard-handley"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/6944024-maynard-handley">Maynard Handley</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes but...<br/>If you're sensible, you'll pick up enough of the backstory (that Miles is crippled but very smart, that he ran a mercenary operation for a t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes but...<br />If you're sensible, you'll pick up enough of the backstory (that Miles is crippled but very smart, that he ran a mercenary operation for a time, etc) but you will miss overtones.<br /><br />I'd recommend starting slightly earlier (not at the very beginning) with The Warrior's Apprentice, which is gripping enough to make you want to learn move about this universe, but not yet starting to become steeped in previously generated lore. If you like that, you can decide whether to keep going forward and jump back to the very beginning.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1919282732" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1919282732" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1919282732?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=scifi">scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1919282732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3271496900668314817"><b>A buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko' rel='nofollow noopener'>Choko</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova' rel='nofollow noopener'>Maria</a>.</b><br/><br/>Miles Vorkosigan graduated from the Military Academy despite his handicap. He hoped for a decent assignment, but his superiors thought he had an insubordination problem, so they decided a good way to fix it is to assign him to a remote place which in this case happened to be a military base on an island in the middle of nowhere, far in the north (read - cold). <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487808810i/22053441._SX540_.jpg' width='460' height='280' alt='Frozen Island' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>First thing Miles did upon arriving was to insult the base Commander - albeit unintentionally. To be fa</span>
  <span id="freeText3271496900668314817" style="display:none"><b>A buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko" rel="nofollow noopener">Choko</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova" rel="nofollow noopener">Maria</a>.</b><br><br>Miles Vorkosigan graduated from the Military Academy despite his handicap. He hoped for a decent assignment, but his superiors thought he had an insubordination problem, so they decided a good way to fix it is to assign him to a remote place which in this case happened to be a military base on an island in the middle of nowhere, far in the north (read - cold). <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487808810i/22053441._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="280" alt="Frozen Island" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>First thing Miles did upon arriving was to insult the base Commander - albeit unintentionally. To be fair the Commander happened to be a real despot even by Barrayan standards, so Miles could not remain neutral for long. <br><br>Miles' adventures on the island constitute a story called Weatherman that was later incorporated in this novel - word by word. <br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487810004i/22053496._SX540_.jpg" width="460" height="330" alt="Station" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The excitement started when the guy was removed from the base. Sufficient to say he ended up saving a couple of planets (including his own) and preventing a couple of wars. He ended up literally in the middle of the excitement without even trying, but getting beaten a lot in the process. My buddy readers mentioned that Miles' immediate superior officer can kiss their career good-by and I completely agree. Superior officers tend to end up trying - and failing - to clean up the mess the guy leaves in his wake.<br><br>The novel won a Hugo Award for Best Novel at the time when good writing and plot were more important than political leaning. To make a long story short the novel is good. Speaking about character development: Miles does first and foremost. I like the way the Barrayan Emperor was shown; unlike his previous appearance he behaved like a human being. Space battles, behind-the-scenes manipulations, people of the future with real human emotions and hopes, Miles overcoming yet another seemingly hopeless situation using just his head, good writing - what else a book need to be called good? Nothing; thus 4-star rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3271496900668314817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=scifi-modern">scifi-modern</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=x-vorkosigan-saga">x-vorkosigan-saga</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer655443028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11630968221447137003"><i>Miles be nimble!<br/>Miles be quick!<br/>Miles jump over <s>the candlestick</s> any situation or dumbass that gets in your goddamn way!<br/><br/>Go, Miles, Go!</i><br/><br/>so Miles finds himself stuck in a miserable freezing arctic station as his reward for graduating from the Barrayar military acadamy with top honors but also with a serious issue of not treating authority with the respect and passivity and obedience that authority apparently deserves. and from the arctic station he finds himself tossed pell-mell, willy-nilly, etc, ri</span>
  <span id="freeText11630968221447137003" style="display:none"><i>Miles be nimble!<br />Miles be quick!<br />Miles jump over <s>the candlestick</s> any situation or dumbass that gets in your goddamn way!<br /><br />Go, Miles, Go!</i><br /><br />so Miles finds himself stuck in a miserable freezing arctic station as his reward for graduating from the Barrayar military acadamy with top honors but also with a serious issue of not treating authority with the respect and passivity and obedience that authority apparently deserves. and from the arctic station he finds himself tossed pell-mell, willy-nilly, etc, right into the middle of a plot teeming with ruthless villains, a young emperor trying to escape his duties, nervous colonies, anxious bodyguards, two mercenary camps, new space gadgets, and reunions galore with characters from prior novels. the novel is fast and fun fun fun.<br /><br />I suppose one take-away from the series is ALWAYS QUESTION AUTHORITY. nice.<br /><br />the character of Gregor le petit emperor really comes into his own here. a beautiful bit of characterization and not a little tragic as well.<br /><br />my favorite part of the novel was the first third, in that freezing arctic station. watching hyperactive Miles practically bounce off of the walls trying to figure out what to do was wonderfully amusing. and the setting was certainly well-rendered. cooooooooold.<br /><br />there is a spicy lil' villainess just like Miles is a spicy lil' hero. she wears some kind of sexy catsuit. or it may be a jumper but I much prefer to imagine it as a catsuit, plus I really wanted to type the word "catsuit". much like Miles, she has a quick and improvisatory way of thinking, always on the fly and always taking advantage of any opportunity she sees. for some reason the novel takes pains to compare Miles and Catsuit, at times even theorizing that if Miles doesn't watch out, he may end up like the amoral Catsuit sometime in the future. ha! as if. equally key to Miles' persona are his decency and his compassion and his refusal to see death as something that just happens so time to move on. those traits are hallmarks of this book and its predecessors as well. Miles ain't gonna turn into no Catsuit! although I do predict that he will eventually tap that Catsuit.<br /><br /><i>this review is a part of a larger piece on the Vorkosigan Saga novels I've read so far, posted on</i> <a href="http://www.shelfinflicted.com/2013/07/the-vorkosigan-saga-by-lois-mcmaster.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelf Inflicted</a></span>

<div id="review_1874231384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1874231384" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1874231384?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=advanture">advanture</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874231384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer290445515804523400"><b>*** 4.25 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with Evgeny and Maria, because we need some FORWARD MOMENTUM!!!</b><br/><br/>This is one of those series that, although it gives us guarantees that the protagonist is going to be OK, since more books, it also gives us a sense of optimism, something I miss in most of contemporary writing. There are some typical sci-fi and adventure tropes, but Miles Vorkosigan is such a great character, that all is forgiven! We root for the young man, who is great despite himself and makes all around h</span>
  <span id="freeText290445515804523400" style="display:none"><b>*** 4.25 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with Evgeny and Maria, because we need some FORWARD MOMENTUM!!!</b><br /><br />This is one of those series that, although it gives us guarantees that the protagonist is going to be OK, since more books, it also gives us a sense of optimism, something I miss in most of contemporary writing. There are some typical sci-fi and adventure tropes, but Miles Vorkosigan is such a great character, that all is forgiven! We root for the young man, who is great despite himself and makes all around him live up to their potential. <br /><br />After finishing the academy, Miles is sent to a post in a frozen island as an officer meteorologist. He is shocked, because he is well aware of his physical inability to do that particular job, since it involves a lot of walking and activities his body is not strong enough to do. Since he is the new guy, mean pranks are part of his daily life. Soon after he gets a handle on his job, some of his fellows start dying and Miles decides to investigate. Of course, this only gets him in trouble and makes his superior a major enemy for life.<br /><br />Miles gets himself reassigned and because he is who he is, all believe he is being favored by the Military leadership because he is Admiral Vorkosigan's son. Miles decides to mind his own business, trying to be a subordinate soldier, but faith and his restless, never asleep brain once again get him in the middle of a potential galactic war. Somehow, the young Emperor Gregor also decides right at this moment to try and run away from his life and heavy responsibilities... Being a ruler does not sit well with him at this point and he runs to the space fleet, which is where he bumps with Miles, who at once just knows he has to keep Gregor safe and get him back home. If only it were that easy... But no, the two of them get themselves in deep trouble and the odds of them getting out alive are slim to none...<br /><br />We also got to see Miles meeting with Elena and his , or not his anymore, mercenaries... It was as melancholy but funny as well, as we thought it would be .. One of the captains has overtaken the command and he is not pleased to have Miles back at all. Who is a friend and who is not is not as easy to know, so the constant worry and paranoia that plagues him is completely justified... <br /><br />Once again this was very exciting, and very satisfying! It feels like a Sci-fi adventure and has a very positive core. I would recommend it to all because I feel there is something for anyone in it!!! And yes, there usually is the happy end and unlikely resolutions, but it is just what this author does so well and we need this optimism in our daily lives!!! I can't wait to read the next one ASAP ☺!<br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and may you always find what you need in the pages of a good book!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="290445515804523400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2018-shelf">2018-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570519810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4473130456345809847">Re-read 2018:<br/><br/>My head spun. Really. It did.<br/><br/>I will not go on record saying that this was anywhere near my favorite Vorkosigan novel, but there is enough plain fun and wild plotting and vibrant characterizations to satisfy any old-school Space-Opera junkie. <br/><br/>I make no excuse. Miles is a superhero. He rides the wave of superheroic Bujoldian coincidence and Miles always happens to be the right person in the right place with the right quippy tongue and the right mind for the job. Even when he isn't. He</span>
  <span id="freeText4473130456345809847" style="display:none">Re-read 2018:<br /><br />My head spun. Really. It did.<br /><br />I will not go on record saying that this was anywhere near my favorite Vorkosigan novel, but there is enough plain fun and wild plotting and vibrant characterizations to satisfy any old-school Space-Opera junkie. <br /><br />I make no excuse. Miles is a superhero. He rides the wave of superheroic Bujoldian coincidence and Miles always happens to be the right person in the right place with the right quippy tongue and the right mind for the job. Even when he isn't. He just happens to have a rather quick imagination and the ability to spin tales that anyone believes.<br /><br />That, I guess, is pretty damn amazing. :)<br /><br />It also says a lot about Bujold. :)<br /><br /><br />Original Review:<br /><br />This was a great fast tale, and satisfying on many levels, but I have a few issues with it. Perhaps it's my same issue with all of the tales. It's plot providence. It ties up all of the side issues quite nicely, true, but it's almost unbelievable. Don't get me wrong, I enjoyed the different sections of the book almost as if it was a collection of short stories, and it really had the feel of just that, but when Miles comes up against his previous commander in the employ of the other mercenaries on pure chance, I went... Huh? He was old guard, and very unlikely to leave his beloved homeland. Perhaps he could be convinced to participate in a coup, but not to work as a mercenary. I might not have had this reaction if he had just been a completely different man, but then, the same level of hate wouldn't have made sense.<br /><br />Sometimes, it's impossible to satisfy readers.<br /><br />That being said, I had a great time reading it and Mile's antagonists were crushed to my great satisfaction. It can only be described as a great yarn. A lot happens, and I even accepted the fantastic chance that brought the Emperor into Miles's care (or neglect) as a funny way to up the stakes. Actually, the emperor kinda stole the show at one point.<br /><br />Actually, a lot of Ms. Bujold's supporting cast tend to steal the show, often. I'm reading all of these with a keen eye on Ivan, too.<br /><br />Very enjoyable!</span>

<div id="review_2280454862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2280454862" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2280454862?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/17240615-the-vor-game">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2280454862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15383895746372375232"><b>3.5 stars</b> as it was slightly better than the last book<br/><br/>Unpopular opinion time: I don't like Miles Vorkosigan.<br/>He's annoying and irritating. He was cute as a little boy at the end of the last book about his parents (Barrayar), what with his physical disadvantage but strong and sharp mind, trying to win over even his grandfather. By now, in his early 20s, his character is less than charming however. <br/><br/>He's supposedly very intelligent, a great strategist like his father, yet I don't see it anywhere. He</span>
  <span id="freeText15383895746372375232" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b> as it was slightly better than the last book<br /><br />Unpopular opinion time: I don't like Miles Vorkosigan.<br />He's annoying and irritating. He was cute as a little boy at the end of the last book about his parents (Barrayar), what with his physical disadvantage but strong and sharp mind, trying to win over even his grandfather. By now, in his early 20s, his character is less than charming however. <br /><br />He's supposedly very intelligent, a great strategist like his father, yet I don't see it anywhere. He stumbles from one situation into another (some his own fault because he's trying to prove himself, some the fault of others who are trying to bully or even outright murder him) and every time he tries to get out of the respective problematic situation, he makes it worse. The truly awful thing, however, is that everyone around him flocks to him and just waits for the oh so brilliant Miles to lead them into disaster (they actually expect him to come up with a plan although at least people like Elena know by now how ridiculous his plans always are and how much he relies on luck). I just don't get it. Sure, there are even more stupid people around (not only on Barrayar which gets mocked for its traditions), but does truly nobody see that Miles isn't actually smart?!<br /><br />So in this second book about Miles and his "adventures" we start with him graduating from the military academy through some political strings that got pulled at the end of the last novel. His first posting is to some Arctic outpost and of course the spoiled little brat complains and whines about not having gotten something more prestigious (actually monologuing about how it might be discrimination which is just privileged noise from someone who thinks he’s owed something). Only when one of his superiors dangles some bait before his nose does he go. *rolls eyes*<br />The Arctic station was actually interesting though it was clear that it wouldn’t last long and how it would fit into later complications.<br />From there, Miles is taken to Imperial Security so as to get him out of the line of fire and, while helping Illyan, he gets framed for murder, arrested and meets the Emperor (who listened to the "brilliant" Miles and thus got himself incarcerated as well) in prison. *sighs*<br />After that, it's a romp through half a galaxy to get the Emperor home safely but since nothing is straight forward with Miles, we meet his mercenaries from the last book (now with "political" problems of their own) as well as a femme fatale.<br /><br />Maybe it's that Bujold is all over the place with Miles' stories. I'm not sure. In the two books about Cordelia and Aral, we had political intrigue and some military space action, but never such a mess as here. Just too many focus points, too many battles for one story. Or it really is me not being able to warm up to Miles.<br />I know he's supposed to be like a superhero but I JUST DON'T BUY IT. Captain America has his strength, Iron Man has his suit, Dr. Strange has magic ... Miles only has his deformity. <br />Don't get me wrong, I love that there was an author audacious enough to make a seemingly disabled person her hero (although he's "just" small and has brittle bones, the rest has been cured by the doctors). <br />Her writing must have been an innovation back in the day as well.<br />However, I just can't connect to Miles because I don't see his supposed brilliance. <br />All I see is him being a burden to everyone precisely because he can NOT pull off heroic deeds, giving everyone a heart attack because he refuses to accept No for an answer, and endangering the people he supposedly loves. Add to that that he showcases hubris and all other marks of a spoiled brat (he's an only child, almost died before birth, so that plus his status on Barrayar and his charming nature as a kid ensured he was fussed over and never learned any boundaries).<br />So yeah, all I want to do is throw him in a small and not very comfortable room for at least a week and give him a good thrashing.<br /><br />I might continue with the series because I was promised it would at least shift from military action to mysteries he needs to solve through wit alone (and maybe Bujold is better with political and social messes than military ones), but I really don't see why this series is so beloved (except for the afore-mentioned innovation factor about a disabled MC back in the day or, in fact, even nowadays).<br />If it wasn't for me reading this one book per month with the SpecFic group, I would have already given up. :/</span>
  <a data-text-id="15383895746372375232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_349490788" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349490788" />
    <a title="Clouds" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds"><img alt="Clouds" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514641128p2/9374686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349490788?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clouds" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clouds" href="/user/show/9374686-clouds">Clouds</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=hugo">hugo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=pub-1990s">pub-1990s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9374686-clouds?shelf=vorkosigan-saga">vorkosigan-saga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349490788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12067979213479079076"><a href='http://www.theaceofclouds.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>Following the resounding success of my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2' rel='nofollow noopener'>Locus Quest</a>, I faced a dilemma: which reading list to follow it up with? Variety is the spice of life, so I’ve decided to diversify and pursue six different lists simultaneously. This book falls into my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=5' rel='nofollow noopener'>HUGO WINNERS</a> list.<br/><br/>This is the reading list that follows the old adage, "if it ain't broke, don't fix it". I loved reading the Locus Sci-Fi Award winners so I'm going to crack on with the Hugo winners next (but only the post-1980 winners, I'll follow up w</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12067979213479079076" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.theaceofclouds.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380317319i/689370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>Following the resounding success of my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=2" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus Quest</a>, I faced a dilemma: which reading list to follow it up with? Variety is the spice of life, so I’ve decided to diversify and pursue six different lists simultaneously. This book falls into my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/332414-reading-lists?chapter=5" rel="nofollow noopener">HUGO WINNERS</a> list.<br><br>This is the reading list that follows the old adage, "if it ain't broke, don't fix it". I loved reading the Locus Sci-Fi Award winners so I'm going to crack on with the Hugo winners next (but only the post-1980 winners, I'll follow up with pre-1980 another time).</b><br><br>Long-running series should, ideally, be read in the internal chronological order. Unfortunately, Maestro <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16094.Lois_McMaster_Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Bujold</a> did not write her epic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40380-vorkosigan-saga" rel="nofollow noopener">Vorkosigan Saga</a> in the obvious order – she’s jumped back and forth in the timeline with each successive book. Under these circumstances, fans that have been with her since the beginning will have experienced the full story in publication order, which also makes perfect sense. Being the contrary and ornery individual that I am, I am reading this wonderful series in neither chronological or publication order, but rather a semi-random and illogical sequence of my own devising! (Faye uses the word ornery a lot in older <a href="http://questionablecontent.net/" rel="nofollow noopener">QuestionableContent</a> issues I’ve been reading and it got lodged in my head.)<br><br>I began with Book Nine (<i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61909.Mirror_Dance" rel="nofollow noopener">Mirror Dance</a>
</i>) and then jumped back to Book Two (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61905.Barrayar" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Barrayar</i>
</a>) – both read as part of my Locust Quest. These stories caught me hook, line and sinker: I declared myself a loyal reserve in the Emperor’s Vorkosigan Fan-Club Army.<br><br>Next, I found my way here to Book Four, (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68483.The_Vor_Game" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>
    <b>The Vor Game</b>
  </i>
</a>) as it was flagged for my attention as a Hugo winner from 1991 (more on that later). And I’ve now been given Books 8, 10 and 11 (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/76811.Borders_of_Infinity" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Borders of Infinity</i>
</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61880.Memory" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Memory</i>
</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61884.Komarr" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Komarr</i>
</a>) as Birthday presents. Hurray!<br><br>I love a big fat series. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40650-discworld" rel="nofollow noopener">Discworld</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40346-the-dresden-files" rel="nofollow noopener">Dresden Files</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40750-the-dark-tower" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark Tower</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40713-saga-of-the-pliocene-exile" rel="nofollow noopener">Pliocine Exile</a>/<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40712-galactic-milieu-trilogy" rel="nofollow noopener">Galactic Milieu</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43939-foundation" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundation</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43318-night-s-dawn" rel="nofollow noopener">Night’s Dawn</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43790-a-song-of-ice-and-fire" rel="nofollow noopener">A Song of Ice and Fire</a>. Catch my drift? To me, the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/40380-vorkosigan-saga" rel="nofollow noopener">Vorkosigan Saga</a> is the best thing I’ve discovered since I began the Locus Quest (and that includes <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/545.Neal_Stephenson" rel="nofollow noopener">Neal Stephenson</a>, who I now adore). It took a great effort of will to not tear into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61905.Barrayar" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Barrayar</i>
</a> the moment it arrived, and another to resist the allure of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68483.The_Vor_Game" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>
    <b>The Vor Game</b>
  </i>
</a> for weeks and weeks until my reading list said I was allowed to! (I’m very strict with my reading lists – once the list is made, the list is boss.)<br><br>Whereas <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61905.Barrayar" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Barrayar</i>
</a> focuses on Miles’ mother around the time of his birth, and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61909.Mirror_Dance" rel="nofollow noopener">Mirror Dance</a>
</i> focuses on Miles’ clone-brother when they’re both in their late twenties. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68483.The_Vor_Game" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>
    <b>The Vor Game</b>
  </i>
</a> focuses exclusively on Miles in his late teens, just after graduating – and more Miles equals more fun! He’s a terrifically likeable lead and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16094.Lois_McMaster_Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Bujold</a> has a real flair for character which isn’t common in sci-fi. <br><br>This is a classic book of three acts. Miles starts in the military, gets assigned to some backwater Arctic camp, and has a massive personality clash with the commander, which gets them both fired. He gets re-assigned as a spy, and out in the field, under-cover, he bimbles around for some time, getting a feel for the territory on one mission before he bumps into his old childhood chum, The Emperor, who is on the lam incognito! Miles has to rescue his friend, foil the intergalactic plot that threatens his home-world, defeat his old Arctic-camp nemesis, and dig some other mercenary buddies out of the hole he left them in during his last adventure! It’s a light-hearted, whirlwind adventure in the best traditions of Space Opera. Miles is a fast talking, faster thinking, marginally psychotic, loveable little scamp!<br><br>It was one of those books where I spent the whole time reading it with a huge grin plastered on my face, and strangers in coffee shops looked at me with a worried squint. (Or maybe they were just curious if it was really ‘sugar’ I was putting in my drink?) <br><br>A quick note on the cover: I seem to have a copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68483.The_Vor_Game" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>
    <b>The Vor Game</b>
  </i>
</a> that was a short-lived edition. I can’t find the correct cover on GoodReads, and I’ve searched high and low on the internet, and the only version I could find anywhere was an e-bay pic of a guy’s hand holding the book. I now cannot even find that! (I shall add a pic to this review when I find my camera). So apparently this is rare – maybe it would be worth something if my copy wasn’t battered to frack. I take my books wherever I go, in whatever pocket they can be crammed – I am not kind to covers and spines.<br><br>Another quick note: After seeing how much I was enjoying this series, my darling wife has now gotten in on the fun, and agrees that Miles is utterly adorable and the books are awesome. We are now a family of Vorkosigan fans together! Double-hurray!<br><br>As far as I can tell you can jump into this series at any point because they’re all superbly written, stand-alone novels as well as linking together into an epic sci-fi adventure series. So you’ve got no real excuses – just grab the first one you spot and get involved!<br><br><b>
  <i>P.S.</i>
</b><br><i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68483.The_Vor_Game%22%22" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vor Game</a> won the 1991 Hugo Award. The Locus Sci-Fi award that year went to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons" rel="nofollow noopener">Dan Simmons</a>' <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77565.The_Fall_of_Hyperion" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fall of Hyperion</a> (which is awesome) and the Nebula went to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/874602.Ursula_K_Le_Guin" rel="nofollow noopener">Le Guin</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13661.Tehanu" rel="nofollow noopener">Tehanu: The Last Book of Earthsea</a> (which I haven't read yet). I've given both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77565.The_Fall_of_Hyperion" rel="nofollow noopener">Fall</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68483.The_Vor_Game" rel="nofollow noopener">Vor Game</a> 5-stars, but of the two I'd give <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons" rel="nofollow noopener">Simmons</a> the nod as an outstanding achievement.</i><br><br><b>After this I read: </b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/326884715" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelmaker</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12067979213479079076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2283936926" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2283936926" />
    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2283936926?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2283936926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11492905062679891568">This review is for my reread of the Vorkosigan Saga with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> during 2017/18. This is the first of the Miles novels that I haven't read before, and there's quite a few from here that will be new to me as well. I originally picked up the series from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61880.Memory__Vorkosigan_Saga___10_' title='Memory (Vorkosigan Saga, #10) by Lois McMaster Bujold' rel='nofollow noopener'>Memory</a>.<br/><br/>Miles Vorkosigan has graduated the Imperial Military Academy and looks set for a bright future of military service as long as he develops some important basic officer skills. To this end he gets sent to a small frozen military ou</span>
  <span id="freeText11492905062679891568" style="display:none">This review is for my reread of the Vorkosigan Saga with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> during 2017/18. This is the first of the Miles novels that I haven't read before, and there's quite a few from here that will be new to me as well. I originally picked up the series from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61880.Memory__Vorkosigan_Saga___10_" title="Memory (Vorkosigan Saga, #10) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Memory</a>.<br /><br />Miles Vorkosigan has graduated the Imperial Military Academy and looks set for a bright future of military service as long as he develops some important basic officer skills. To this end he gets sent to a small frozen military outpost in the middle of nowhere. Being Miles though, trouble soon follows, in this case with an embittered veteran military commander who resents the "softness" of the peacetime military. Letting a "mutant" serve only emphasizes his prejudice, so Miles is in trouble from the start. But actions Miles is forced to take lead him into space for another encounter with the mercenary company that he formed in the previous book and he's forced to deal with consequences of his earlier actions and a brand new interstellar situation.<br /><br />The first section of this where Miles is on Kyril Island for his miserable first posting I thought was brilliant. It encapsulates a lot of what I love about the series including the rich world-building (for example, the discussion of the Barrayaran minority populations) as well as Miles's ability to win people over by being both empathic and competent at his job. It also does a great job at illustrating the boundaries of Miles has and what he's willing to sacrifice for those.<br /><br />The second section with the Hegen Hub was less successful in my opinion. A lot of it is more of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61906.The_Warrior_s_Apprentice__Vorkosigan_Saga___2_" title="The Warrior's Apprentice (Vorkosigan Saga, #2) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warrior's Apprentice</a> with regards to the Dendarii Mercenaries, but much of the rest of it is outrageous coincidences followed by situations where the plot of the story and the antagonists as well seem to set Miles up for victory. The whole thing feels very railroaded, although it's nice to see Miles growing up a bit and facing the consequences of his actions. (More on that much later in the series).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11492905062679891568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_643873035" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/643873035" />
    <a title="Stuart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart"><img alt="Stuart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452041473p2/9456990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/643873035?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stuart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stuart" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart">Stuart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=future-war">future-war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=satirical-humorous">satirical-humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=humanistic-sf">humanistic-sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=military-sf">military-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer643873035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4483822279299492620"><b>The Vor Game: Another madcap Miles adventure</b><br/>This was another fast-paced, well-balanced, and very enjoyable adventure centering on Miles, his cousin Ivan, the Dendarii mercenaries, some very villainous villains (including a very clever and calculating femme fatale), and even young Emperor Gregor thrown into the mix. Once again Miles finds himself stumbling from one disastrous situation to another, always managing to squeak by his wits alone, knowing how to manipulate and outsmart rather than over</span>
  <span id="freeText4483822279299492620" style="display:none"><b>The Vor Game: Another madcap Miles adventure</b><br />This was another fast-paced, well-balanced, and very enjoyable adventure centering on Miles, his cousin Ivan, the Dendarii mercenaries, some very villainous villains (including a very clever and calculating femme fatale), and even young Emperor Gregor thrown into the mix. Once again Miles finds himself stumbling from one disastrous situation to another, always managing to squeak by his wits alone, knowing how to manipulate and outsmart rather than overpower, and being incredibly lucky again and again. <br /><br />The improbable coincidences pile up towards the end, stretching reader credibility, but in a sense that is part of the fun. We know how unlikely it would be in a "serious SF story" for these things to happen without the main characters getting blasted by a nerve disruptor, being spaced, or vaporized in a space battle, but the fact that Miles and Ivan can weasel their way through scrape after scrape is a bit like a really well-written TV comedy. What elevates Bujold's stories of Miles and his friends is that her characters are both three-dimensional and believable, even if their situations are not. There is always an emotional element to the story, including unrequited love and feelings of inferiority from our mad genius hero, and the frustrations of Emperor Gregor who chafes at his stifling position. It all adds up to a cracking good yarn, and when you remember that it is part of a much larger Miles Vorkosigan Saga that works as a greater tapestry, it is really impressive what Lois McMaster Bujold has achieved, and her huge fan base attests to this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4483822279299492620" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16980043480699521304">Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko' rel='nofollow noopener'>Choko</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Evgeny</a>. Even though I have read this book before many times I stayed up half the night (giggling and sometimes laughing out loud and waking the family) to finish it because I couldn't stop. <br/><br/>The fi</span>
  <span id="freeText16980043480699521304" style="display:none">Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko" rel="nofollow noopener">Choko</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a>. Though not really because this time I finished before they even started. <br /><br />Returning to this series is always like coming home and this time was no exception. It's a great way to just relax and forget about the real world. Because Miles just sweeps you away on his mad adventure. Even though I have read this book before many times I stayed up half the night (giggling and sometimes laughing out loud and waking the family) to finish it because I couldn't stop. <br /><br />The first half of the book is a bit boring. Miles is send to Kyril Island - a frozen piece of land in the middle of nowhere. But since this is miles he manages to get himself in all kinds of trouble. Including with his commanding officer the very first time they meet! Miles has a talent for making enemies out of his commanding officers :) And for ruining their careers. Eventually his morals and big mouth get him out of Camp Permafrost. There are some political ramifications of his actions because he is his father's son and there are way too many people that want the old Admiral dead and buried.<br /><br />Miles receives a second chance, this time as part of an ImpSec operation that puts him in contact with his old fleet of mercenaries. Needless to say, that wasn't Illyan's plan but when Miles is involved plans go out the window/airlock. This is the moment when things get interesting and from that point on it's a mad dash all over the Hegen Hub and it's adjoining space. To make things worse Miles is suddenly stuck with Gregor, who has decided that he doesn't want to be Emperor and just ran away. I actually sympathize with Gregor. He is stuck with a job he doesn't really want, is scared that he will fuck up and as a result millions if not billions will pay the price, is a prisoner of his own security force and is always expected to act a certain way. He is playing a role forced on him and has played it all his life. To the point where he doesn't even know himself outside of that role. For the first time ever he has a chance to get to know himself outside of the artificial environment of Vor life and see what he is really made off. I loved seeing this more vulnerable side of him because he is usually just part of the background of the series and when he has page time he is usually in his Emperor mode. <br /><br />In a way this is the beginning of a new chapter for the series and for the next several books we're embarking on a trip with Admiral Neismith and the Dendarii Mercenaries. And with Manic Miles on the helm it's one hell of an adventure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16980043480699521304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344263917?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344263917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15885876495085632718">This is the second of the Miles Vorkosigan books, though it's listed as the forth in the family saga. I was/am very impressed. My rating here is a considered one and I'm very close to a 5 here. I can't quite go there as there were a few false notes (I'll mention later) but all in all an excellent book and a great read. I'll say here in the first paragraph that I wholeheartedly recommend this one. <br/><br/>So, what's good and what's bad? Well, you will find what I've come to believe is Lois McMaster Bujol</span>
  <span id="freeText15885876495085632718" style="display:none">This is the second of the Miles Vorkosigan books, though it's listed as the forth in the family saga. I was/am very impressed. My rating here is a considered one and I'm very close to a 5 here. I can't quite go there as there were a few false notes (I'll mention later) but all in all an excellent book and a great read. I'll say here in the first paragraph that I wholeheartedly recommend this one. <br /><br />So, what's good and what's bad? Well, you will find what I've come to believe is Lois McMaster Bujold's "long suit" her strong point and that's characterization. The people have depth and they are consistent. She writes about them as if they are people she knows and she's simply relating their story. The novel picks up roughly at the point the last one ended (Miles has go to the academy and we come in as he's about be assigned his first post) and Miles launches off on a series of new adventures. <br /><br />The false note I mentioned is that a few times I felt we'd sort of circled back (no details until a spoiler tag). But that wasn't really true and the storytelling is so good as to overshadow any slight or temporary false step. The story is a page turner having a nice thought out plot enlivened with lots of action. There is some great dialog and that isn't always the case even with good novels. Here there are lucid dialogs that give plot exposition and needed details without being dry. There are also many laugh out loud moments here and I enjoyed it thoroughly.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ My mention of a circular plot here was because when we circled back to the mercenaries, saw the return of Admiral" Naismith (whom I assume we haven't seen the last of) and the reawakening (so to speak) of Miles' unrequited love story. But we moved on and got an original story very quickly and a very good one at that.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So, as I said, a highly recommended read and I'm already planning to get to the third/fifth novel in the series. </span>

          </span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer954571960054600218">Young Miles is back. He’s completed his training at the Academy and he’s hoping to get posted on a space battleship. But Miles has a problem with subordination and to prove he is worthy to serve he is required by his superiors to demonstrate he can do just that ie serve - in some backwater Arctic station for six months.<br/><br/>So then Miles serves out his time in humility before being assigned to the pride of the Barrayan fleet <i>The Prince Serg</i> and.....<br/>yeah that didn’t happen. That would be totally borin</span>
  <span id="freeText954571960054600218" style="display:none">Young Miles is back. He’s completed his training at the Academy and he’s hoping to get posted on a space battleship. But Miles has a problem with subordination and to prove he is worthy to serve he is required by his superiors to demonstrate he can do just that ie serve - in some backwater Arctic station for six months.<br /><br />So then Miles serves out his time in humility before being assigned to the pride of the Barrayan fleet <i>The Prince Serg</i> and.....<br />yeah that didn’t happen. That would be totally boring. It’s more like Mile gets to trot and plot all over the galaxy fighting space mercenaries, spying on potential enemies, command set piece space battles and you can bet there is a whole lot of usurping/insubordination involved.<br /><br />What I appreciated about this book is that we pretty much have the same Miles I loved from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61906.The_Warrior_s_Apprentice__Vorkosigan_Saga__3_" title="The Warrior's Apprentice (Vorkosigan Saga #3) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warrior's Apprentice</a>. What I didn’t like so much about this book was that we pretty much have the same Miles I loved from The Warrior's Apprentice. Most of Mile’s character development happened last book. And we had the pycho/sociopathic batman, Bothari. We had Miles ordering torture and having peoples cybernetic insets ripped out their heads. We had Miles storming spaceships and developing his own fleet. We had Miles struggling with the morality of his actions.<br /><br />We don’t really get that much in this book. In this book Miles has no psychopaths under his command doing psychopathic things and very few questions of conscience. It felt like we got the Miles as he was at the end of the last book, which was fine because I do like that Miles and his interactions with Gregor and his various commanders was priceless. But I am looking forward to the next books building on Miles character and career as he gets older.<br /><br />This is more a 3.5 stars for me. I can’t bring myself to give it a 3 so its<br /><br />4 stars<br /></span>

    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2735898019?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/17240615-the-vor-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-female">author-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=20xx-laser">20xx-laser</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2735898019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17821667780542570143"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I think this is probably my favorite book of the series so far. After a bit of a slow start I really enjoyed the rest of it.<br/><br/><b>Audiobook:</b> Grover Gardner does another great job. He's made some of the less interesting books easier to get through. He doesn't do many voices but he seems like a great fit for Miles.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>I've always been someone who prefers to read long-running series in publication order rather than chronological or "recommended" order. For this series that h</span>
  <span id="freeText17821667780542570143" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I think this is probably my favorite book of the series so far. After a bit of a slow start I really enjoyed the rest of it.<br /><br /><b>Audiobook:</b> Grover Gardner does another great job. He's made some of the less interesting books easier to get through. He doesn't do many voices but he seems like a great fit for Miles.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />I've always been someone who prefers to read long-running series in publication order rather than chronological or "recommended" order. For this series that has meant a bit of up and down. This is the sixth book I've read and most of the other five were in the 3-3.5 range. This was a solid 4. <br /><br />I definitely enjoy Miles as a character. I'm a little uncertain where this book slots in compared to some of the others I've read. It seems like it's set before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/296182.Brothers_in_Arms__Vorkosigan_Saga___5_" title="Brothers in Arms (Vorkosigan Saga, #5) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Brothers in Arms</a>. I guess that would be the benefit of reading these chronologically rather than publication order. All I know is I seem to enjoy him more and more as the series goes on.<br /><br />From the description I had thought we were going to spend time with him during the academy. I love a good school trope. However it turns out this essentially starts with his graduation. I found the beginning a little slow but once it got going, I was hooked.<br /><br />I thought there was a lot of good character development. I also enjoyed the stuff with Gregor. I'm a little fuzzy on the details about Miles history with the Dendari fleet, but I feel like I haven't yet read about his first encounter with them yet.<br /><br />Overall this was a solid book, and since I already own <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61905.Barrayar__Vorkosigan_Saga___7_" title="Barrayar (Vorkosigan Saga, #7) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Barrayar</a>, I'll probably jump into that soon. I'm a bit reluctant since that's set after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61903.Shards_of_Honour__Vorkosigan_Saga___1_" title="Shards of Honour (Vorkosigan Saga, #1) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">Shards of Honour</a> which I didn't particularly enjoy, but the consensus seems to be that it's a much better book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17821667780542570143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1371015961" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1371015961" />
    <a title="Gary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30706026-gary"><img alt="Gary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465615148p2/30706026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1371015961?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gary" href="/user/show/30706026-gary">Gary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1371015961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer492839478861988780">The Vor Game was a re-read for me, though my first experience with the novel is from a quarter century ago basically another lifetime. It seemed like the right book to dive into this week because the Hugo awards are today, and this was the first "real time" Hugo winner I read. 14-year-old me had read Hugo winners before (Dune, Rendezvous with Rama, Ender's Game), but at the time I was reading those well after they had won; The Vor Game was the first novel I read because it had JUST won the Hugo.</span>
  <span id="freeText492839478861988780" style="display:none">The Vor Game was a re-read for me, though my first experience with the novel is from a quarter century ago basically another lifetime. It seemed like the right book to dive into this week because the Hugo awards are today, and this was the first "real time" Hugo winner I read. 14-year-old me had read Hugo winners before (Dune, Rendezvous with Rama, Ender's Game), but at the time I was reading those well after they had won; The Vor Game was the first novel I read because it had JUST won the Hugo. I remember liking it well enough, but not well enough to keep reading Bujold - until a couple of months ago when I picked up The Warrior's Apprentice and loved it. I guess Bujold was a one-off for teenage me because the book didn't quite fit what teenage me thought was "great" sci-fi (Herbert, Asimov, Clarke, etc.). My literary tastes were not yet refined to admire the deft plotting and characterization that Bujold excels at. I just wanted BDO's and planet-conquering messiahs and all that sort of stuff. Also, teenage brains aren't well suited for moral grey areas and nuances. Barrayaran hierarchy was hostile toward differently-abled and gays (among other things) and I had both of those in my family. Lump that in with the war crimes in its recent past, and why am I rooting for these guys again? Empires and dynasties are supposed to be toppled and wiped away! What is this gradual social change nonsense!<br />Reading these books now (and I'm pretty sure I will be reading all of them) I still have a bit of an ideological problem with the world Bujold has built, as much as I'm loving being immersed in it. She may be sharply critical of conservative Barrayaran society, and it's nice to see a bit of old school feminism at work, but even if Bujold pokes little holes in the feudal, aristocratic society she created, her narratives (up to this point in the series at least) still tend to promote, justify and reinforce the privileged status of its Vor class, the very system that created (and still benefits from) those injustices and inequalities in the first place.<br />Oh well. She's hardly alone in telling these kinds of stories, and this isn't the first time politically-conscious adult me has enjoyed the hell out of one, nor will it be the last.<br />And again, with this years Hugo ceremony just a few hours away, it's nice to recall the simpler, gentler times of yore, when the Hugos were about celebrating quality writing, rather than about a bunch of sneering internet trolls with axes to grind holding the award hostage to PREVENT good writing from being celebrated.</span>
  <a data-text-id="492839478861988780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6483616791785451823" style="display:none"><b>“Very good. But your most insidious chronic problem is in the area of . . . how shall I put this precisely . . . subordination. You argue too much.” <br />“No, I don’t,” Miles began indignantly, then shut his mouth.</b><br /><br />Ah, another visit with Miles Vorkosigan/Naismith! That incredible bundle of energy, that intellect struggling to slow down to regular human speed. His problems with being the smartest guy in the room, but with physical limitations.<br /><br />In many ways, Miles is like a jazz musician—he knows strategy (the melody) inside &amp; out. When a new situation is thrown at him, he is able in incorporate it into his playing and take the strategy song to new places. <br /><br />My favourite line? One of his captors at one point asks, “How many people <i>are</i> you?”<br /><br /><b>Book 264 of my Science Fiction &amp; Fantasy Reading Project.</b><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1488062281948937549">Great reader, tangled web, & Miles is like a spastic spider running through it all. It's a lot of fun as Miles deals with his insubordination issues - not particularly well as most would guess. He does try hard, though. It's not his fault they give him the wrong orders. (His words, not mine.)<br/><br/>It's a series & if you want to find out more about it, I suggest you read it in chronological order. The list is here:<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/98254-vorkosigan-saga-chronological'>http://www.goodreads.com/series/98254...</a><br/><br/>It's much better than the published order. Bujold</span>
  <span id="freeText1488062281948937549" style="display:none">Great reader, tangled web, &amp; Miles is like a spastic spider running through it all. (His words, not mine.)<br /><br />It's a series &amp; if you want to find out more about it, I suggest you read it in chronological order. Bujold has done a marvelous job filling in the cracks &amp; her writing has gotten better all the time.<br /></span>

<div id="review_3184370741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3184370741" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10818276-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341872613p2/10818276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3184370741?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/10818276-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35557325-the-vor-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=vorkosigan-series-challenge">vorkosigan-series-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=netgalleyreaders2020">netgalleyreaders2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10818276-lee?shelf=war">war</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3184370741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9638639551869655285">This is my fav Miles so far. (I think I might be saying this after every book!) I thought there was a good mix between action and political intrigue, humour and poignancy, and a standalone plot if you wanted to read this out of order but still the forward momentum of the overarching series plot and formation of the characters.<br/><br/>The book’s beginning sequences were fantastic. Miles’s first posting after graduating from military academy is at an isolated outpost at Barrayar’s arctic circle. He is sen</span>
  <span id="freeText9638639551869655285" style="display:none">This is my fav Miles so far. (I think I might be saying this after every book!) I thought there was a good mix between action and political intrigue, humour and poignancy, and a standalone plot if you wanted to read this out of order but still the forward momentum of the overarching series plot and formation of the characters.<br /><br />The book’s beginning sequences were fantastic. Miles’s first posting after graduating from military academy is at an isolated outpost at Barrayar’s arctic circle. He is sent there as a meteorology tech and soon butts heads with the station’s commander. He also manages to come across a dead body. <br /><br />This section felt like an opening sequence in a movie - like a James Bond beginning or the Empire Strikes Back Hoth scene. It had heaps of action and mystery and, although it might not have been completely necessary to the main plot, it did offer a lot of additional characterisation. (I just read it was originally a separate novella, so that explains its feel to some degree.)<br /><br />The action then moves to space when a new series of events has Miles meeting up with the fleet of mercenaries he created in Warrior’s Apprentice. Of course, in amongst the action is a plethora of <br /> important themes. LMB always seems to tackle difficult subjects effortlessly; weaving topics into the plot organically without coming across as preachy. She also always seems to be way ahead of her time. This was published in 1990 and yet she covers a lot of current topical issues - men's health and wellbeing being the most notable. <br /><br />In this universe many characters are members of minority groups but, for the most, they aren't treated differently. I guess the great irony is that Miles is the only one who is treated differently and labelled [incorrectly] as a mutant.<br /><br />The other thing I really liked about this book was the Miles/Gregor dynamic. (Gregor being the emperor of Barrayar who, up until this book, has been discussed quite a bit but rarely featured.) <br /><br />There are sooooo many books out there who have men in this type of relationship (quasi brother relationship) depicted in a negative way. I mean, how many times do we have the male characters who grew up in the same house/shared a parent etc become enemies? One is quite often the villain and one the hero. So many... Even Harry Potter for goodness sake! I just really appreciated that Miles and Gregor acted like they were normal brothers. Even though a fair amount of characters suspected Miles would betray Gregor and attempt to usurp him, Gregor himself never did. (It's also a lovely little reminder that, despite the constant rumours otherwise, Gregor also knows Aral is forever loyal to his position as emperor.) I liked all their scenes together and thought it was a great example of male friendship.<br /><br />My favourites from previous books Aral and Illyan are featured for a fair amount of time but unfortunately Cordelia continues to take a backseat.<br /><br />Looking forward to the next in this series though.<br /><br />5 out of 5 <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9638639551869655285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
