<div id="review_2399802963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2399802963" />
    <a title="Joanka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20233424-joanka"><img alt="Joanka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476184344p2/20233424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2399802963?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanka" href="/user/show/20233424-joanka">Joanka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=usa">usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=fantasy-scifi-and-co">fantasy-scifi-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=women">women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20233424-joanka?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2399802963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6131005638853747873">If you have some idea about my reading preferences you know that I adore stories about some secluded places, especially when they are cold and when a group of people is closed there this way or another and the interactions between them become tense and not so obvious. That’s why I <i>loved</i> the beginning of “The Vor Game.” It was everything that I like and then some. I liked the idea of Miles having to work for his dreamt of job, I liked reading about his learning process and mistakes, and the whole</span>
  <span id="freeText6131005638853747873" style="display:none">If you have some idea about my reading preferences you know that I adore stories about some secluded places, especially when they are cold and when a group of people is closed there this way or another and the interactions between them become tense and not so obvious. That’s why I <i>loved</i> the beginning of “The Vor Game.” It was everything that I like and then some. I liked the idea of Miles having to work for his dreamt of job, I liked reading about his learning process and mistakes, and the whole idea of a mysterious military base in the middle of nowhere. I liked the intrigue and I liked the conclusion. Sadly, that was only 1/3 of the book or maybe even less.<br /><br />Don’t get me wrong. This an interesting novel, quite exciting at times and it contains absolutely loveable interactions between Miles and his father, which I love to pieces. The characters I began to like in the previous volumes appear here as well and it was nice to read about them (especially one fanboy, I mean, man I get you. Totally.) And it’s always rewarding to read about Simon Illyan. I read it quickly, had fun and even sacrifice my precious sleep to finish it on a weekday. That means something.<br /><br />But. There were… too many adventures. Too many events I couldn’t really get into, some new characters that I couldn’t make myself care about till the end (but I started to like the emperor that I finally got to know more!). Also, I can turn a blind eye to too unreal coincidences when they add lots of fun factor and are connected with my favourite characters. But when they make little sense and concern some no-names (well, almost, come one)… Not so much. Yes, there are some really precious scenes and by all means the book is worth reading. I just hoped for more, I think. I don’t care that much about planets, I prefer reading about people.<br /><br />Also, Miles, dear, could you please never ever again speak to any woman you are even slightly attracted to? Pretty please? As much as I liked Miles, his relations with female characters are… embarrassing or simply exasperating. I hope it’s just a phase. I must admit, however, that Miles had moments in this volume when my liking was tried greatly. Some kinds of behavior were acceptable or maybe understandable and excusable when he was a teenager but there they made me uneasy. Maybe the problem lies on my side but there were moments when I sighed and it wasn’t a sigh of satisfaction.<br /><br />Either way, of course I will read the next parts and to be honest I can’t wait to do so. I hope that Miles will grow up to be a better person and I almost count hours before jumping into another Vorkosigan stories.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6131005638853747873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Oleksandr Zholud" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Oleksandr Zholud" href="/user/show/4743119-oleksandr-zholud">Oleksandr Zholud</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3185615598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14852743876858347627">This is the fifth (chronologically) novel of Vorkosigan saga. It won Hugo in 1991. I read is as a part of the Vorkosigan challenge in February 2020 at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/474371-hugo-nebula-awards-best-novels' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hugo & Nebula Awards: Best Novels</a> group.<br/><br/>Miles Vorkosigan finished the Naval Academy and dreams about an officer position on one of the ships. Instead he is sent to a frozen island as a meteorologist, “to check how he can operate under stress”. The infantry training camp is a dumping ground for disgraced officers, drunkards and other undesirables. </span>
  <span id="freeText14852743876858347627" style="display:none">This is the fifth (chronologically) novel of Vorkosigan saga. It won Hugo in 1991. I read is as a part of the Vorkosigan challenge in February 2020 at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/474371-hugo-nebula-awards-best-novels" rel="nofollow noopener">Hugo &amp; Nebula Awards: Best Novels</a> group.<br /><br />Miles Vorkosigan finished the Naval Academy and dreams about an officer position on one of the ships. Instead he is sent to a frozen island as a meteorologist, “to check how he can operate under stress”. The infantry training camp is a dumping ground for disgraced officers, drunkards and other undesirables. Moreover, Miles is instantly disliked by locals, bot as an outsider and ‘mutant’. Once again he has to prove his worth.<br /><br />Like the previous volume, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61906.The_Warrior_s_Apprentice__Vorkosigan_Saga___2_" title="The Warrior's Apprentice (Vorkosigan Saga, #2) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">The Warrior's Apprentice</a>, it is filled by daring and risky adventures, ‘running on a staircase that falls apart’. Some situations are extremely unlikely but nevertheless they make a great story.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14852743876858347627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_520828516" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/520828516" />
    <a title="Anders" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14054706-anders"><img alt="Anders" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420457294p2/14054706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/520828516?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anders" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anders" href="/user/show/14054706-anders">Anders</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14054706-anders?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer520828516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer844457824809020559">I enjoy reading Buljold, and when starting The Vor Game I had just finished the wonderful The Mountains of Mourning. I also like Miles Vorkosigan as the protagonist. He is funny, smart, easy to like, yet far from perfect, which makes him interesting. Finally, I also love a well told Space Opera. <br/><br/>Space opera is a subgenre of science fiction that emphasizes romantic, often melodramatic adventure, set mainly or entirely in outer space, usually involving conflict between opponents possessing advance</span>
  <span id="freeText844457824809020559" style="display:none">I enjoy reading Buljold, and when starting The Vor Game I had just finished the wonderful The Mountains of Mourning. I also like Miles Vorkosigan as the protagonist. He is funny, smart, easy to like, yet far from perfect, which makes him interesting. Finally, I also love a well told Space Opera. <br /><br />Space opera is a subgenre of science fiction that emphasizes romantic, often melodramatic adventure, set mainly or entirely in outer space, usually involving conflict between opponents possessing advanced technologies and abilities.. Perhaps the most significant trait of space opera is that settings, characters, battles, powers, and themes tend to be very large-scale.<br /><br />In The Vor Game there are plenty of all these tings. Bujold's writing, Miles the protagonist, and grand scale adventurous science fiction. It's even a Hugo and Nebula award winner, and a fun read you can easily enjoy. <br /><br />However, for me it didn't quite deliver. Given the above that is surprising. Why is this?<br /><br />First, it's like two or three short stories made into one book. The first story has potential, but never reaches it, and the way the two stories are tied together is beyond belief. I have no problem accepting light speed travel, battles in space, stabile wormholes between worlds, but a leaking plot I can not accept. The fact that Miles travels through several wormholes, only to randomly meet the same people he met in the first part of the book <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ including being thrown into the same cell as the emperor of his home planet Barrayar  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, is a bit too much to accept for me.<br /><br />The last part of the book has everything you would want in a space opera, but at times it feels like Bujold thought: how much trouble can I get the protagonist in, and how often? She pretty much says the very same thing in the afterword to the book. This seems a bit too convenient, and also too easy to predict. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[At the end, we rush through a space battle, which for Bujold is poorly written, only for everything to be solved in no time at the conclusion of the battle. A bit steep when the mighty Cetagandans attack, and a fleet of old mercenary ships with a crew of 5000 in total goes without serious losses, before they are bailed out by all the mighty powers in the area. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />I will read more Bujold, and more of the Vorkosigan Saga, but this only gets a three star rating. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="844457824809020559" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1290222591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1290222591" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7356691-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325898058p2/7356691.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1290222591?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/7356691-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1290222591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7315590336994325489">I'm marking this four stars only because Cordelia's Honor was five, and this isn't as good as that one (those two), but in a general range of excellence, five out of five, would read again.<br/><br/>"Miles, in one breath you just plotted to kill the emperor, cuckold him, accused your father of homosexuality, and suggested patricide. What's your encore?!"<br/>"I wish I knew!"<br/><br/>Jasmine and Stephanie reviewed this book saying they would die in a war for Gregor. I would absolutely die for Gregor. Poor little king. T</span>
  <span id="freeText7315590336994325489" style="display:none">I'm marking this four stars only because Cordelia's Honor was five, and this isn't as good as that one (those two), but in a general range of excellence, five out of five, would read again.<br><br>"Miles, in one breath you just plotted to kill the emperor, cuckold him, accused your father of homosexuality, and suggested patricide. What's your encore?!"<br>"I wish I knew!"<br><br>Jasmine and Stephanie reviewed this book saying they would die in a war for Gregor. I would absolutely die for Gregor. Poor little king. Trapped in a world that eats its children. <br>I ADORE that Miles was like, "this is me out of my depth, I can't be the only one who knows this. You need to talk to someone." "Who?" "My mother." <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433091252ra/15048634.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I love at the end of the book when Miles and Gregor talk a circle around Illyan and Illyan realizes he's lost, and instead of being angry he's like... "I'm gonna get to retire! We've done it, Aral! We made competent leaders out of these children!" It hearkens back to (or ahead to, if you read by publication order) Barrayar when the entire goal is to make a better world for the children. They were trying to get Gregor to the throne a better man than his father, to let Miles live and have possibility and be more than his disabilities, to allow Elena to be more than the sins of her father (both victim and abuser), and to let Ivan be Ivan. Cordelia, Aral, Illyan, all the rest, kept pushing forward, and with every step they were willing to die for their kids, and now here they are: it's not a perfect world, but their kids have caught the vision and are pushing forward too, trying to take the best of what their parents were and leave the worst. And it's <i>hard</i>. But they'll do it anyway.<br>uuuuuuuuraaaaarrrrrrrrrg I love it so much!<br><br>Plus the book was so FUN! SO FUN!<br>Bring on Cetaganda!<br><br>2nd read, April 2019.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1555940698ra/27397464.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Last time I was pretty focused on the meta, if the above review is anything to go on. This time around was just fun. I love this book, and I thoroughly enjoyed the re-read.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1555940698ra/27397465.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9758179190301446506">Vegetarian fare. That is, there's no meat to it.<br/><br/>It's entertaining, but there are so many ghosts in this machine that it needs an exorcist. I was going to say that Miles Vorkosigan is the biggest Mary Sue ever. But he's not, because he doesn't have talent, he just has more luck than anybody else in the universe!<br/><br/>Now I face a quandary. I'm reading the Hugo winners. There are two more books in the series for which she's won Hugos! I have the same problem with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14032.Connie_Willis' title='Connie Willis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Connie Willis</a>. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77773.To_Say_Nothing_of_the_Dog__Oxford_Time_Travel___2_' title='To Say Nothing of the Dog (Oxford Time Travel, #2) by Connie Willis' rel='nofollow noopener'>To Say Nothing of the Dog</a></span>
  <span id="freeText9758179190301446506" style="display:none">Vegetarian fare. That is, there's no meat to it.<br /><br />It's entertaining, but there are so many ghosts in this machine that it needs an exorcist. I was going to say that Miles Vorkosigan is the biggest Mary Sue ever. But he's not, because he doesn't have talent, he just has more luck than anybody else in the universe!<br /><br />Now I face a quandary. I'm reading the Hugo winners. There are two more books in the series for which she's won Hugos! I have the same problem with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14032.Connie_Willis" title="Connie Willis" rel="nofollow noopener">Connie Willis</a>. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77773.To_Say_Nothing_of_the_Dog__Oxford_Time_Travel___2_" title="To Say Nothing of the Dog (Oxford Time Travel, #2) by Connie Willis" rel="nofollow noopener">To Say Nothing of the Dog</a> was excellent; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24983.Doomsday_Book__Oxford_Time_Travel__1_" title="Doomsday Book (Oxford Time Travel #1) by Connie Willis" rel="nofollow noopener">Doomsday Book</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7519231.All_Clear__All_Clear___2_" title="All Clear (All Clear, #2) by Connie Willis" rel="nofollow noopener">All Clear</a> were unreadable: so do I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6506307.Blackout__All_Clear___1_" title="Blackout (All Clear, #1) by Connie Willis" rel="nofollow noopener">Blackout</a>, which also won a Hugo.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WVlDpSXUee9LFHxEnos6ssGowzRekIu2Qght80BkBU+u3EcFIE7AaDJROMKHCfAPRDKqOEQVkatOrnwtNgD2hw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4619357023194084569">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br/><br/>Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestse</span>
  <span id="freeText4619357023194084569" style="display:none">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br /><br />Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestselling Vorkosigan Saga. Her work has been translated into over twenty languages.<br /><br />A listing of her awards and nominations may be seen here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bujold">http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bu...</a><br /> <br />A listing of her interviews is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Author_Interviews">http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Auth...</a><br /><br />An older fan-run site devoted to her work, The Bujold Nexus, is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.dendarii.com/">http://www.dendarii.com/</a><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

        $('bookCover_61884').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_61884').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_61884').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
